  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer7221278234592613243">They say that diplomacy is a gentle art. That its finest practitioners are subtle, sophisticated individuals for whom nuance and subtext are meat and drink. And that mastering it is a lifetime's work.   <span id="freeText7221278234592613243" style="display:none">They say that diplomacy is a gentle art. That its finest practitioners are subtle, sophisticated individuals for whom nuance and subtext are meat and drink. And that mastering it is a lifetime's work. But you <i>do</i> need a certain inclination in that direction. It's not something you can just pick up on the job.<br /><br />Which is a shame if you find yourself dropped unaccountably into a position of some significant diplomatic responsibility. If you don't really <i>do</i> diplomacy or haven't been to school with the right foreign bigwigs or aren't even sure whether a nod is as good as a wink to anyone, sighted or otherwise, then things are likely to go wrong. It's just a question of how badly...</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/649770-do-these-books-discworld-need-to-be-read">Do these books (discworld) need to be read in order? Or are they stand along stories?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_649770'><a id="like_count_community_question_649770" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/649770?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F63720.The_Fifth_Elephant">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/649770-do-these-books-discworld-need-to-be-read">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/649770-do-these-books-discworld-need-to-be-read">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4596610-nicola"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1291056380i/4596610._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4596610-nicola">Nicola</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">They don't need to be read in strict order but it helps if you have some idea of the structure of the world and who the people are for the later books<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">They don't need to be read in strict order but it helps if you have some idea of the structure of the world and who the people are for the later books otherwise I've heard it can be quite confusing.<br /><br />Terry Pratchett has several sub-series' inside the over arching series of 'Discworld' and they are: 1. Rincewind the cowardly and inept wizard (he starts off the series with books #1 and #2); 2. The Witches (start with Wyrd sisters for this one; 3; The Guards (start with Guards! Guards!) and 4. Death (start with Mort) and possibly 5. The Wizards although these often concern other characters as well. He also has the Tiffany Aching series which is aimed more at junior readers but I personally love them.<br /><br />Quite a few of his books overlap characters so there are very few entirely stand alone books even if they aren't from one of the 4 main groups. Probably the best stand alone would be Small Gods.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1569024-i-posted-a-review-wasn-t-easy-to-find-how">I posted a review, wasn&#39;t easy to find how to do this, but what does this function do and mean please?

There are &#39;spoilers&#39; contained in the review... sorry wasn&#39;t sure how the &quot;Hide entire review because of spoilers&quot; feature works?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1569024'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F63720.The_Fifth_Elephant">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1404450006i/32761625._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra">Cassandra</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hiding the entire review means that, on the list of reviews, yours says something like <i>this review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To vi</i><a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hiding the entire review means that, on the list of reviews, yours says something like <i>this review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it, <u>click here</u></i> <br />(which, when clicked, reveals the full review)<br /><br />If you have a few spoilers in the review, you can use the "hide spoiler" function: type "&lt;spoiler&gt;" where it starts and "&lt;/spoiler&gt;" where it finishes. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18422162421113958570">Diplomaticing anything out of the downplaying of an incident around a just ideologically not completely worthless and overrated cult object.<br/><br/>The fine art of not going to war or, if so, at least sophisticated, with style, culture, and the right documents bureaucracy wants to see before the slaughter fun can start, that´s what diplomacy is for. Already ridiculous in real life, because the madness of tradition, ideology, and dogmas makes each country a special, unique mental asylum, it gets even mor</span>
  <span id="freeText18422162421113958570" style="display:none">Diplomaticing anything out of the downplaying of an incident around a just ideologically not completely worthless and overrated cult object.<br /><br />The fine art of not going to war or, if so, at least sophisticated, with style, culture, and the right documents bureaucracy wants to see before the slaughter fun can start, that´s what diplomacy is for. Already ridiculous in real life, because the madness of tradition, ideology, and dogmas makes each country a special, unique mental asylum, it gets even more hilarious when Samuel Vines has got the job.<br /><br />The object of saber rattling is just a strange looking object in a, maybe fictional, fictional story because, just as with diplomacy, there is no logic included except the underlying economic and market forces Pratchett is infamous for exposing and making fun of. His works include more differentiated, wise, and true analysis than whole subfields of wacky fringe sciences Alfred Nobel never wanted prices to be given for under his name so that they had to wait a while, strangely and completely coincidentally until the beginning of the rise of neoliberalism with extraordinarily and suspiciously many prices given to the university of Chicago and it´s bonkers boys, to get the dry and boring pipe dreams rolling. <br /><br />How the true masters behind the kings and presidents ruled, rule, and will rule by manipulating the predictable and primitive primate instincts of their voters, in this case to use different cultural norms to let them fight good, old divide et impera style, is a fascinating topic and that it´s so easy to satirize too, because of it´s inherent sick and illogical nature that ought one let start thinking about why these anachronistic systems are still so strong in each seemingly democratic system.<br /><br />Even the original, more obvious Scone of Stone metaphor, playing with the idea of any kind of cult object, is still big, which really makes one wonder about cultural evolution, until one realizes that the human brain hasn´t really developed that much over the last tens of thousands of years, so maybe it still needs some time to jump over the apes with smartphones line. <br /><br />The reasons for laughter are always tabus and pain, but jumping from just giggling to realizing what´s behind the hilariousness is a step just a few are willing to take, because it would mean critical self analysis and possible change of mentality, so they prefer to better just keep smiling without digging too deep inwards toward the reasons why their cognitive dissonances start ringing.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/TheFifthElephant">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><br />This one is added to all Pratchettian reviews:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibenwelt-Romane#Liste_der_Romane">https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibe...</a> <br />The idea of the dissected motifs rocks, highlighting the main real world inspirational elements of fiction and satire is something usually done with so called higher literature, but a much more interesting field in readable literature, as it offers the joy of reading, subtle criticism, and feeling smart all together.</span>

<div id="review_20972094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20972094" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1116185-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241138579p2/1116185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20972094?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/1116185-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1116185-kristen?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20972094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3441230528812171528">I know that many have stated that there had been a decline in his writing as time goes on… I personally would have to disagree. There is a change in his writing; however I feel that it has been for the better. As his book have progressed, he has leaned less toward the quick giggle and insane rush of nonsense and more toward a satirical plot with darker edges and the giggles interspersed within the story rather than his jokes running the story.<br/><br/>The Fifth Elephant is one of Pratchett’s more plot dr</span>
  <span id="freeText3441230528812171528" style="display:none">I know that many have stated that there had been a decline in his writing as time goes on… I personally would have to disagree. There is a change in his writing; however I feel that it has been for the better. As his book have progressed, he has leaned less toward the quick giggle and insane rush of nonsense and more toward a satirical plot with darker edges and the giggles interspersed within the story rather than his jokes running the story.<br /><br />The Fifth Elephant is one of Pratchett’s more plot driven novels, there isn’t a giggle or a chortle on every page as with some of his others. I have always liked the Guard’s series for this reason, I like a good plot. If you have not read a discworld book before, I wouldn’t advise this be your starting place, instead I would start at the beginning of whichever series it is you want to read. This being part of the Guards Series I would start with “Guards Guards” which although it is by no means the strongest entry in the series, it is a good introduction to the lead character of Samuel Vimes and his crew. Each of the following books adds additional characters who become major players in the later books. The characters truly grow through each of the books and I think that having read the previous in the series will increase your enjoyment of this one.<br /><br />Quick Summary: A strange theft and murder occur in Ankh-Morpork, and just as the Watch is about to investigate, The Patrician sends Vimes and his wife off to Uberwald to attend the coronation of the new Dwarfish Low King as ambassadors. While street hardened Vimes has to start learning about politicking, Angua disappears… and Carrot decides to go after her, unfortunately her trail leads to Uberwald, land of vampires, werewolves, and Dwarves who rarely come to the surface. As Sam Vimes always says – A cop will always find a crime, the origins of the strange crimes in Ankh-Morpork also lead back to Uberwald and the coronation ceremony. Vimes finds himself attempting to not only play politician and ambassador, but also detective to sort out the truth before the Dwarves are thrown into a bloody civil war.<br /><br />The summary sounds a bit dark doesn’t it? Well this, much like “Carpe Jugulum,” is a darker more plot driven novel, but the humor is still there. Cheery accompanies Vimes back to her homeland as military attaché and unfortunately her modern ways cause issues amongst the more traditional dwarves of Uberwald. Detrius the Troll attends as the cultural attaché, unfortunately in Uberwald the trolls and dwarves have been at war for over a hundred years… then throw in Angua’s noble yet slightly psychotic werewolf family, and a Vampire clan that’s on the wagon from drinking human blood… everyone is moving their chess pieces and poor Sam has to figure it all out. Sybil has a much larger roll in this story than in the past, and her personality really begins to develop. This book is funny, full of action, and intrigue… who stole the Scone? Who murdered the prophylactics maker? Where is the fake stone? Who is behind it all? The opposing Dwarves? The Werewolves? The Vampires? Or is it someone from within? <br /><br />Although I didn’t laugh nearly as much during this book, I found myself truly enjoying the read much more than some of the others. If I were to try to tell you what “The Color of Magic” was about… I really couldn’t other than to say it was about running away… True, I enjoyed it immensely, but this had a plot, a meaning, and more to learn from, I think this is an excellent addition to the Discworld series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3441230528812171528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2021766250" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021766250" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021766250?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021766250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6860820617238252974">“So this is diplomacy.  It’s like lying, only to a better class of people.”<br/><br/>So says Sam Vimes / Terry Pratchett in his 1999 novel The Fifth Elephant. Discworld fans also know that this 24th Discworld book was a return of the wonderfully entertaining City Watch sub series. In this edition, Pratchett has the Duke of Ankh go to Uberwald on a diplomatic mission for which Vimes is uniquely qualified.<br/><br/>Pratchett had previously visited the vampires in Uberwald in the 23rd Discworld book, 1998’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34541.Carpe_Jugulum__Discworld__23__Witches__6_' title='Carpe Jugulum (Discworld #23; Witches #6) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carpe Jugu</a></span>
  <span id="freeText6860820617238252974" style="display:none">“So this is diplomacy.  It’s like lying, only to a better class of people.”<br><br>So says Sam Vimes / Terry Pratchett in his 1999 novel The Fifth Elephant. Discworld fans also know that this 24th Discworld book was a return of the wonderfully entertaining City Watch sub series. In this edition, Pratchett has the Duke of Ankh go to Uberwald on a diplomatic mission for which Vimes is uniquely qualified.<br><br>Pratchett had previously visited the vampires in Uberwald in the 23rd Discworld book, 1998’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34541.Carpe_Jugulum__Discworld__23__Witches__6_" title="Carpe Jugulum (Discworld #23; Witches #6) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Carpe Jugulum</a>. Here, readers finally get to see first-hand the creepy gothic Discworld region referenced in many Discworld books as a home of dwarfs, vampires, werewolves and Igors.<br><br>Like all Discworld books, Sir Terry mixes in lots of humor and action with thought provoking themes and musings. Here we have fun with truth and diplomacy, eastern European folklore, royalty and conflict between orthodox and reform elements, as well as progressive politics. One aspect of this book that was an unusual surprise was the idea of Ankh-Morpork as a kind of pluralistic, multi-cultural haven, almost an ugly America; but more hospitable in some respects than the old country.<br><br>Not as funny as some other Discworld novels, but complete with Pratchett’s inimitable style and humor, this is still very enjoyable.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547604291i/26923328._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="255" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6860820617238252974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1092791323" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1092791323" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8595029776025691972"><i>“Let me see if I've got this right,' said Vimes. 'Überwald is like this big suet pudding that everyone's suddenly noticed, and now with this coronation as an excuse we've all got to rush there with knife, fork and spoon to shovel as much on our plates as possible?'<br/>'Your grasp of political reality is masterly, Vimes. Your lack only the appropriate vocabulary.”</i><br/><br/><i>“Vetinari was throwing him amongst the wolves. And the dwarfs. And the vampires. Vimes shuddered. And Vetinari never did anything without a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8595029776025691972" style="display:none"><i>“Let me see if I've got this right,' said Vimes. 'Überwald is like this big suet pudding that everyone's suddenly noticed, and now with this coronation as an excuse we've all got to rush there with knife, fork and spoon to shovel as much on our plates as possible?'<br />'Your grasp of political reality is masterly, Vimes. Your lack only the appropriate vocabulary.”</i><br /><br /><i>“Vetinari was throwing him amongst the wolves. And the dwarfs. And the vampires. Vimes shuddered. And Vetinari never did anything without a reason.”</i><br /><br />So <b>His Grace, His Excellency, The Duke of Ankh; Commander Sir Samuel Vimes </b> (aka my chosen Literary Husband) is going to the dangerous, faraway country of Überwald, where there is no Law, only The Lore, as Ambassador of Ankh-Morpork. <br /><br />He is of course eager (ahem) and ready to "hand round the cucumber sandwiches like anything" and to get the hang of (or just to hang) diplomacy, but his policeman's nose and insticts tell him that something is rotten in the state of Überwald and it is not the hot baths. <br /><br />First of all, the Scone of Stone, this most famous and priceless of dwarf bread, having seated the Low Kings of the Dwarfs for some fifteen hundred years, goes missing. The Low King cannot be Low King without this artifact. <br /><br />The werewolves with their mad leader, Wolfgang, who happens to be Sgt. Angua's brother, are definitely up to something. <br /><br />And where do the vampires, lead by the Lady Margolotta (and possibly former love interest of Lord Vetinari hmmm, hmmm) come into this picture?<br /><br />Vimes has a lot to figure out while incidentally also running for his life and those of others, possibly.<br /><br />And what has a cherry orchard with 3 spinsters got to do with it? Not much, admittedly, but I certainly appreciated the literary hint. And the humour and poignancy and Vimes, of course... I did tell you about.... yes, I did, didn't I? OK.<br /><br />A great book in the Watch series (well, all books are great in the Watch series) and one I return to again and again with pleasure.<br /><br />And Vimes meeting DEATH.. PRICELESS:<br /><br /><br />He took his hands off the oars and pulled in the mooring rope. If I make a couple of loops, he thought, I can strap the axe on to my back.<br />He had a mental picture of what could happen to a man who plunged into the cauldron below a waterfall with a sharp piece of metal attached to his body.<br />GOOD MORNING.<br />Vimes blinked. A tall dark robed figure was now sitting in the boat.<br />'Are you Death?'<br />IT'S THE SCYTHE, ISN'T IT? PEOPLE ALWAYS NOTICE THE SCYTHE.<br />'I'm going to die?'<br />POSSIBLY.<br />'Possibly? You turn up when people are possibly going to die?'<br />OH, YES. IT'S QUITE THE NEW THING. IT'S BECAUSE OF THE UNCERTAINTY PRINCIPLE.<br />'What's that?'<br />I'M NOT SURE.<br />'That's very helpful.”</span>

<div id="review_2804492536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2804492536" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2804492536?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552146166" href="/book/show/797191.The_Fifth_Elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2804492536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8937593493790274251">So much is happening in this 24th <i>Discworld</i> novel.<br/><br/>A dwarf king will be crowned in Überwald so the Patrician is sending Sam Vimes in his capacity as duke to participate in the coronation ceremony. As, no doubt, planned by the Patrician, sending Vimes ensures that justice will be done. Because there is a theft, a murder, diplomacy, a lot of very impolite werewolves, "vegetarian" vampires and plots. Oh, and then there are regular wolves, Gaspode, and some members of the Watch (Carrot, Angua, Detrit</span>
  <span id="freeText8937593493790274251" style="display:none">So much is happening in this 24th <i>Discworld</i> novel.<br><br>A dwarf king will be crowned in Überwald so the Patrician is sending Sam Vimes in his capacity as duke to participate in the coronation ceremony. As, no doubt, planned by the Patrician, sending Vimes ensures that justice will be done. Because there is a theft, a murder, diplomacy, a lot of very impolite werewolves, "vegetarian" vampires and plots. Oh, and then there are regular wolves, Gaspode, and some members of the Watch (Carrot, Angua, Detritus and Longbottom).<br><br>I very much liked how the spotlight shone on characters that had been explored only marginally until now. Thus, Carrot was not the unfailing hero here so Angua got to shine much more. Angua's family history was also a nice touch. Just like Longbottom's complicated status in this sometimes backwards dwarf kingdom. Most wonderful was to see Lady Sybil stepping up and taking <s>bars</s> matters into her own, very capable, hands.<br> <br>And then there was this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559248596i/27594525.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yes, that is Detritus the troll with his "crossbow". *lol*<br>The action scenes here were not only thrilling but also hilarious in their details. Just like the conversations between the Patrician and Leonard or Fred Colon panicking because he had to take over as captain.<br><br>Sir Terry addressed a lot of themes in this volume, such as the ongoing gender identity amongst some dwarves, religion, traditions, facing political and social changes (the different meanings of "changing with the times") ... we even have organ donation. Well, body-parts donation as a theme. *lol*<br><br>As usual, this was like putting on your favourite piece of clothing. Like coming home. I was thrown off by the new audiobook narrator (Nigel Planer had quit and Stephen Briggs had taken over) a little at first and wasn't actually happy by the end either, but maybe it will get better in the future. I'm just used to the different voices of the different characters (especially Detritus). However, being with Sam Vimes and the other members of the Watch is always great, and it was still a wonderful addition to the series, very entertaining while also critically examining aspects of human nature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8937593493790274251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_858266732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858266732" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858266732?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061051579" href="/book/show/325379.The_Fifth_Elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=humorous-fiction">humorous-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858266732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1698770114325445352">Aw, man!<br/><br/>First the Scone of Stone goes missing. Then Angua disappears and Carrot is off to find her. With Sam Vimes on his way to the coronation in Uberwald, that leaves Fred Colon as Acting Captain of the Watch. The horror, the horror! He annoys everyone and makes a general mess of everything...not to mention that his "principles" make him reluctant to investigate the death of a local manufacturer of rubber preventatives. <br/><br/>Sound confusing? It's not. At least, not yet. <br/><br/>Throw in some assorted dwarf</span>
  <span id="freeText1698770114325445352" style="display:none">Aw, man!<br /><br />First the Scone of Stone goes missing. Then Angua disappears and Carrot is off to find her. With Sam Vimes on his way to the coronation in Uberwald, that leaves Fred Colon as Acting Captain of the Watch. The horror, the horror! He annoys everyone and makes a general mess of everything...not to mention that his "principles" make him reluctant to investigate the death of a local manufacturer of rubber preventatives. <br /><br />Sound confusing? It's not. At least, not yet. <br /><br />Throw in some assorted dwarfs, trolls, wolves and werewolves, all with their own foibles and agendas, and your head may start to spin a bit.<br /><br />Welcome to Discworld where just about anything can happen...and so, it DOES.<br /><br />I was definitely NOT expecting to meet a certain three sisters who talk a lot about the weather and how much better things used to be. One of these dissatisfied ladies has a suggestion:<br /><br /><b>"You know, I bet if we cut down the cherry orchard, I'm sure we could put in a roller skating rink---"</b><br /><br />They also reluctantly offer to help clothe a nearly nude Vimes:<br /><br /><b>"We have the gloomy and purposeless trousers of Uncle Vanya..."</b><br /><br />This is one terrific outing by Pratchett, who even manages to offer some marital advice:<br /><br /><b>Sam Vimes could parallel process. Most husbands can. They learn to follow their own line of thought while <i>at the same time</i> listening to what their wives say. And the listening is important , because at any time they could be challenged and must be ready to quote the last sentence in full. A vital additional skill is being able to scan the dialogue for telltale phrases, such as "and they can deliver it tomorrow" or "so I've invited them for dinner" or "they can do it in blue, really quite cheaply."</b><br /><br />Learn this valuable skill, guys and gals. Yes, it does work for women, too. I use this technique when my husband's going on and on about his day at work, and believe me, it's a lifesaver!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1698770114325445352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1167299761691118412">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br/><br/>In the country of Uberwald the Low King of the dwarfs is about to be crowned.   <span id="freeText1167299761691118412" style="display:none">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br /><br />In the country of Uberwald the Low King of the dwarfs is about to be crowned. As the second largest dwarf city in the world Ankh-Morpork needs to seen a representative and the Patrician decides on the Duke of Ankh, Commander Sam Vimes. But Uberwald is a country in careful balance between vampires, werewolves and dwarfs and politics are afoot, particularly as Vimes includes Sergeant Detritus and Corporal Cheery Littlebottom in his entourage. Trolls and dwarfs still fight each other in Uberwald, and a female dwarf is something that more traditional dwarfs get upset about.<br /><br />This has long been one of my favourite books in the series. All the Watch books are basically Vimes books, but his supporting cast really get to play here. Lady Sybil gets the first really great outing since she was initially introduced, and we finally see some progress in whatever is going on between Angua and Carrot. With Carrot backgrounded for most of this Detritus and Cheery also really get to shine, and this is a brilliant book for Cheery.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386404-richard?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1316434593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15776655462314659000">8.5/10<br/><br/>Back to form after a disappointing outing last time with Jingo. This is another stonking effort in the Watch sub-series making it hard for me not to start raving about them to people and tell them if they’ve not read them then they need to pick them up and get cracking!<br/><br/>Plot wise things are shaken up again. I did groan a little when I learnt that Vimes would yet again be leaving Ankh-Morpork for a distant land like in the last novel, but this time it proved to be an inspired choice and work</span>
  <span id="freeText15776655462314659000" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />Back to form after a disappointing outing last time with Jingo. This is another stonking effort in the Watch sub-series making it hard for me not to start raving about them to people and tell them if they’ve not read them then they need to pick them up and get cracking!<br /><br />Plot wise things are shaken up again. I did groan a little when I learnt that Vimes would yet again be leaving Ankh-Morpork for a distant land like in the last novel, but this time it proved to be an inspired choice and worked really well adding in some new fresh characters and adding extra layers to a few we already know. A fish out of water in a new land but yet Vimes still evolves into someone to be reckoned with whilst discovering a plot to start a civil war, solving a murder and handling a union strike at home (well he didn’t do anything with that but he sorted it in spirit). <br /><br />There was a much darker feel to this book than I’ve previously seen in the Discworld novels (even the ones with Death which could become quite morbid if you think about it) but Terry Pratchett has enough humour in his locker to add some light relief along the way to keep things on this side of crazy batshit. I think the whole story had enough to put this at the top of my favourite Watch novels and up there with some of the better reads of the last few years (high praise indeed!). <br /><br />It’s good to read these as a light break in between other reads but this one shows these shouldn’t be underestimated and really do work very well as a great book on many levels. My ignorance on some of the humour is quite apparent too but that isn’t the author’s failing, that’s the English Education System (definitely not me and my lack of wanting to learn at school). Looking forward to the next one now but unhappy that there are only 3 left in the sub-series to go.<br /><br />If you like this try: “Going Postal” by Terry Pratchett</span>

<div id="review_864356400" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864356400" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/864356400?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385409957" href="/book/show/833503.The_Fifth_Elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close">not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=i-vant-to-drink-your-blood">i-vant-to-drink-your-blood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=shop-on-your-own-shelves-2018">shop-on-your-own-shelves-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864356400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7473059363524266085"><blockquote>
  <b>“Well, he thought, so this is diplomacy. It's lying, only for a better class of people.” <br/><br/>"It was funny how people were people everywhere you went, even if the people concerned weren’t the people the people who made up the phrase 'people are people everywhere' had traditionally thought of as people."</b>
</blockquote><br/>I keep going back and forth over whether this should get the fifth star, and that back and forth is what's keeping it at four (for now), but this is my favorite of these books since <i>Hogfather</i>. I v</span>
  <span id="freeText7473059363524266085" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“Well, he thought, so this is diplomacy. It's lying, only for a better class of people.” <br /><br />"It was funny how people were people everywhere you went, even if the people concerned weren’t the people the people who made up the phrase 'people are people everywhere' had traditionally thought of as people."</b>
</blockquote><br />I keep going back and forth over whether this should get the fifth star, and that back and forth is what's keeping it at four (for now), but this is my favorite of these books since <i>Hogfather</i>. I very well may change my mind at any time and increase the rating. It didn't *quite* have the emotional oomph I like from these books in order to get the fifth star, but it was so much fun, and there was a little oomph, so . . . ugh, whatever. This book is great. Goodreads, give us half stars.<br /><br />We are going back to Uberwald in <i>The Fifth Elephant</i>, and this time Captain Samuel Vimes of the Ankh-Morpork City Watch is going with us. Except he's not going as Captain, he's going as the Duke of Ankh-Morpork, a title he does his best to forget he owns. The dwarfs are crowning a new Low King, and the rest of the Disc has cottoned on to the potential wealth of resources that might be obtained by befriending the monstrous and strange creatures that live there, which as well as dwarfs, also includes werewolves and vampires. They live in relative peace with one another, but Uberwald is a very different place than Ankh-Morpork, so Vimes is sent with his wife Lady Sybil, and three natives of Uberwald from the Watch: Angua (werewolf), Cheery Littlebottom (dwarf), and Detritus (troll).<br /><br />Things of course start to go wrong immediately, and Vimes is the perfect POV on it all. His mix of practical cleverness, stubbornness, and cultural in/sensitivity make for an extremely entertaining read. The dwarfs' Scone of Stone, which they need for the coronation (a play on the historical <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stone_of_Scone" rel="nofollow noopener">Stone of Scone</a>) has been stolen, as well as the replica housed in the dwarf Museum of Bread in Ankh-Morpork, and Vimes is determined to solve both crimes, whether or not his help is wanted (it's not; sort of).<br /><br />My favorite parts of this were all to do with Vimes interacting with dwarf society, back home or in Uberwald. Pratchett uses the dwarfs (and to a lesser extent the other two races) to comment on lots of real life issues, like immigration, and old country vs. new country, which all leads to lots of (humorous) meditation on when to hold to tradition, and when to evolve. Vimes is always a good lens for this, because he *wants* to understand, and he mostly succeeds, but there's always a level of permanent befuddlement there that leads to a lot of really good one-liners. As he himself would be the first person to point out, he's a small-picture kind of guy.<br /><br />I've been working through these book since I was eighteen, and I kind of sort of thought I'd never run out, because there are SO MANY of them. But I think I've finally reached the point where my brain realizes there is an end point to Discworld. I only have seventeen more left. Maybe I should slow my pace from three a year to one or two. On the other hand, there's always re-reading.<br /><br />[4.5 stars]</span>
  <a data-text-id="7473059363524266085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1895691846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1895691846" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1895691846?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895691846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2433588989852664814"><i>The Fifth Elephant</i> is the fifth book in the <i>Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. As I’ve mentioned in previous reviews, my enjoyment of the <i>Watch</i> books has grown as the series has progressed. With this book however, I wasn’t as entertained by it as I had been by the last couple. I’m not sure if it was the book or if it was me, since I was traveling on business this week and I was surprisingly tired even though it wasn’t a particularly strenuous trip. There were also a lot of distractions during the bul</span>
  <span id="freeText2433588989852664814" style="display:none"><i>The Fifth Elephant</i> is the fifth book in the <i>Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. As I’ve mentioned in previous reviews, my enjoyment of the <i>Watch</i> books has grown as the series has progressed. With this book however, I wasn’t as entertained by it as I had been by the last couple. I’m not sure if it was the book or if it was me, since I was traveling on business this week and I was surprisingly tired even though it wasn’t a particularly strenuous trip. There were also a lot of distractions during the bulk of the time I spent reading it.<br /><br />As with the last couple of <i>Watch</i> books, this is one of the more plot-driven <i>Discworld</i> books. Vimes is sent on a “diplomatic” mission to Uberwald to attend a coronation but he ends up with a mystery to solve. The plot was somewhat interesting, but not riveting. The humor was there, but it didn’t often have me laughing out loud. While the other characters all had their parts to play, Vimes had the largest role and maybe that’s part of the reason I didn’t enjoy it as much. I usually think the other characters in this subseries are more entertaining.<br /><br />So, all in all, I found this book to be pretty average. I enjoyed it, but it probably isn’t one of the books I’ll look back on with any particular fondness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2433588989852664814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3413525853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3413525853" />
    <a title="Di Maitland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland"><img alt="Di Maitland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585661189p2/112155925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3413525853?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Di Maitland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Di Maitland" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland">Di Maitland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552146166" href="/book/show/797191.The_Fifth_Elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=diplomacy">diplomacy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=titled-characters">titled-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=non-humans">non-humans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=in-library">in-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=werewolves-vampires-witches">werewolves-vampires-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=law-enforcement">law-enforcement</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=detective">detective</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3413525853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11377765815333179521">I hate writing reviews for Terry Pratchett books. I just feel so bad about giving a Pratchett book 3*s. The trouble is, they're not bad. I would hate for people to get the impression that I don't like them. I do. It's just that I like particularly aspects of them a lot, and some aspects of them only a little.<br/><br/><b>The 'A Lot' Parts</b><br/>Pratchett's world-building is to die for. You could play bingo with the number of different creatures he manages to include in his books. In The Fifth Elephant, we had:<br/>- Hum</span>
  <span id="freeText11377765815333179521" style="display:none">I hate writing reviews for Terry Pratchett books. I just feel so bad about giving a Pratchett book 3*s. The trouble is, they're not bad. I would hate for people to get the impression that I don't like them. I do. It's just that I like particularly aspects of them a lot, and some aspects of them only a little.<br /><br /><b>The 'A Lot' Parts</b><br />Pratchett's world-building is to die for. You could play bingo with the number of different creatures he manages to include in his books. In The Fifth Elephant, we had:<br />- Humans (including Nobby Nobbs, a pseudo-human)<br />- Dwarves (including Carrot, a pseufo-dwarf), gnomes, imps and nano-imps<br />- Werewolves, wolves and talking dogs<br />- Trolls and gargoyles<br />- Vampires, zombies, golems, igors and DEATH<br />Each race has a well thought-out history and culture which is usually delightfully ludicrous. Take Constable Buggy Swires, for example. A six-inch tall gnome who uses condoms as raincoats:<br /><blockquote>"After a bit of work wi' yon scissors, ye won't find a better mackintosh in the whole city"</blockquote><br />Or take the dwarves, the stars of this show, who mine, not rock, but the fat deposits of a giant, long-dead and buried elephant.<br /><br />Races aside, Pratchett's characters are wonderfully developed. Vimes, already one of my favourite characters, is only improved in my opinion by his partnership with his wife, Sybil, who describes him as "not a gentleman, thank goodness, but a gentle man." Likewise, Carrot, another favourite, is lent depth through his relationship with Angua. They're not sappy, but their bond is no less because of it.<br /><blockquote>'"Do you think I'm proud of this? I've got a brother who's a sheepdog!"<br />"A <i>champion</i> sheepdog," said Carrot earnestly. [...]<br />"You actually mean that, don't you? You really do. And if you'd met him it wouldn't worry you, would it. To you everyone's a person. I have to sleep in a dog basket seven nights a month and that doesn't worry you either, does it?"'</blockquote><br /><br /><b>The 'Little' Parts</b><br />The plot. There was a plot, I just wasn't that interested in it. There wasn't enough compelling me to keep turning the pages and I found it all too easy to put the book down. It was nice to revisit the characters and to see how things had developed from previous books (though I've certainly not read them in order or consecutively), but once I'd checked in, I was happy to go away again.<br /><br />And so we end up with a 3* rating. Will I be reading more Discworld books? OF COURSE. They're good for a laugh, infinitely inventive, and home to some of my favourite characters. Who cares if I pick them up and put them down as I fancy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11377765815333179521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1234970701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234970701" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143969-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409947508p2/1143969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1234970701?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1143969-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6567848-the-fifth-elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=i-heard-you-like-footnotes">i-heard-you-like-footnotes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=dysfunctional-families">dysfunctional-families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=great-villains">great-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=pratchett-reads">pratchett-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234970701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15843546820307210131">I want to embark on an chronological Discworld in memoriam reread, but for now I started by revisiting <i>The Fifth Elephant</i> for Reasons. Gosh, I love this book: diplomacy and spycraft set in an old Germanic continent, in which the Gothic runs rife, the forests are deep and dark and dangerous, and there are supernatural beasties around every corner. (The races to get home before sunset being a fun Uberwaldean hobby is just <i>the cutest</i>.)<br/><br/>What struck me the most about rereading this book is that while </span>
  <span id="freeText15843546820307210131" style="display:none">I want to embark on an chronological Discworld in memoriam reread, but for now I started by revisiting <i>The Fifth Elephant</i> for Reasons. Gosh, I love this book: diplomacy and spycraft set in an old Germanic continent, in which the Gothic runs rife, the forests are deep and dark and dangerous, and there are supernatural beasties around every corner. (The races to get home before sunset being a fun Uberwaldean hobby is just <i>the cutest</i>.)<br /><br />What struck me the most about rereading this book is that while it delivers a super fun and enjoyable plot with memorable characters, a really vivid setting, and a perfect lampooning of Gothic/horror stereotypes, Terry Pratchett's values are also interwoven throughout. The story involves sexism and feminism and SMASHING THE PATRIARCHY, open-mindedness and acceptance, mixed-race and adoptive and expatriate cultural issues, slow social change and moving with the times, the advancement of technology and its effects, the dangers of conservatism &amp; racism, definite overtones of Nazism and their quest for racial purity -- meanwhile featuring good, solid people with good values who fight for each other and who stand up for what's right, even down to the very small stories, like being a Good Dog. I love the big political backdrop as much as I love the relationship struggles between Carrot and Angua, the hints of Vetinari and Margolotta (I SHIP IT LIKE BURNING), Vimes and Sybil and their adorable domesticity and his growth, all set against a locked-room mystery.<br /><br /><i>Everyone</i> is moving with the times, dragged kicking and screaming into the century of the fruitbat, from teetotaller vampires to rebellious Igors with Modern Scientific Ideas, to dwarf feminists, to the clacks towers blazing a trail across the continent and shrinking the world. This book is about setting aside old and dangerous conservatism while still staying true to your cultural roots and traditions -- to the thing, and the whole of the thing.<br /><br />Plus, Uberwald is one of my favourite settings anywhere, and I'm super into werewolves so the fact that they're the main villains of the piece delights me. I'm so into the von Uberwalds, you guys, they are so freakin' great. I think this book is one of my favourites of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15843546820307210131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of fantasy novels and other Terry Pratchett novels</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134958805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13624005797979158536">Published : 6/11/2008<br/>Author: Terry Pratchett<br/><br/>Another amazing book written by an amazing author! In this book we see the characters Nobby Nobbs, the wonderful Sam Vines, Havelock Vetinari , Carrot Ironfoundsson plus many more amazing characters. The setting of this novel is Uberwald. This is book 5 in the City Watch part in the Discworld novels. <br/> This is another great book that transports us into the world that he has created, we go on the adventure with the characters, get to know them and enjoy </span>
  <span id="freeText13624005797979158536" style="display:none">Published : 6/11/2008<br />Author: Terry Pratchett<br /><br />Another amazing book written by an amazing author! In this book we see the characters Nobby Nobbs, the wonderful Sam Vines, Havelock Vetinari , Carrot Ironfoundsson plus many more amazing characters. The setting of this novel is Uberwald. This is book 5 in the City Watch part in the Discworld novels. <br /> This is another great book that transports us into the world that he has created, we go on the adventure with the characters, get to know them and enjoy the adventure with them. Terry Pratchett has a way with words that paints a vivid picture in the readers mind, even though I didn't find this book as funny as the others it is still a brilliant incredible story. I really really enjoyed reading this book. <br /> The words that Terry Pratchett uses are so brilliant and powerful that they can make you feel like you are there, make you picture the Discworld like it is actually a real place and that all the people features are real too. It is one of them kind of books that you can sit down and read and not notice that hours have gone by without you moving, eating, sleeping, blinking or doing anything at all! This book really does caught your attention and hooks your mind not letting you go it keeps bringing you back to reading it. This to me is a sign of a really great book!<br /> Each of the characters add something brilliant too the novel, they add in the humor and they add depth too the novel making it feel extremely realistic too the reader. It is definately one that can be read many times without it getting bored, and it is also one that I will treasure always and never be able to part with it. I love Terry Pratchett books and I particularly love this book!</span>

<div id="review_1813287557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813287557" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813287557?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552146166" href="/book/show/797191.The_Fifth_Elephant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813287557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18178315323164999169"><b>Another City Watch Story</b><br/>28 November 2016<br/><br/>	There was a time that I loved the adventures of Constable Carrot, Captain Vimes, and Nobby Nobbs, but is seems as of late the stories are starting to become really, really dry. Okay, maybe there are other factors, but I really don't seem to be able to get into the Pratchet books any more, to the point that I am starting to find them quite boring. Sure, there are probably people out there that will crucify me because I have spoken blasphemy, but fortunatel</span>
  <span id="freeText18178315323164999169" style="display:none"><b>Another City Watch Story</b><br />28 November 2016<br /><br />	There was a time that I loved the adventures of Constable Carrot, Captain Vimes, and Nobby Nobbs, but is seems as of late the stories are starting to become really, really dry. Okay, maybe there are other factors, but I really don't seem to be able to get into the Pratchet books any more, to the point that I am starting to find them quite boring. Sure, there are probably people out there that will crucify me because I have spoken blasphemy, but fortunately those people are actually few and far between. As it happens a number of people I have spoken to have suggested that by this time, which is actually book number 24, is that the fun, wonder, and humour of the Discworld series is starting to reach its used by date.<br /><br />	The thing is that it seems that we only have two sets of protagonists in the stories – The Witches and the City Watch. In fact it seems that at this stage we are alternating between them. Actually, as I was reading this book I suddenly realised that it has actually been quite a while since Rincewind and the Wizards have been a major focus of a story (though I do believe there is one more coming up, but that is basically it). Sure, Rincewind did at first annoy me but the character sort of started to grow on me to the point that the last book that I can remember I quite enjoyed (I believe it was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47994.The_Last_Continent__Discworld___22__Rincewind__6_" title="The Last Continent (Discworld, #22; Rincewind #6) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Last Continent</a>, but the one set in Discworld's version of China was also quite good). However, now we just have the Watch trampsing off somewhere to do what the watch does, and in fact there is only a passing mention of a Fifth Elephant – the title actually doesn't have anything to do with the story itself.<br /><br />	What has happened is that Vimes is sent off to the Uberwald, which is a land inhabited by Dwarves, Werewolves, and Vampires, to strike a trade deal with the dwarves for fat (which was deposited there when the fifth elephant that carried the disc crashed into the area – pretty dumb idea I feel) that is buried beneath the land. However, while they are there the Scone of Stone, a mystical artifact that is important for the coronation of the low king of the dwarves as been stolen, and it is up to Vimes, and Constable Carrot, to get to the bottom of the situation.<br /><br />	Sure, Pratchet is still parodying aspects of our world, such us what is termed the Theseus Paradox – if an object's component parts are completely replaces is it still the same object. The classic example in my mind involves <a href="http://www.thatsmelbourne.com.au/PlacesToGo/CooksCottage/Pages/Cookscottage.aspx" rel="nofollow noopener">Captain Cook's Cottage</a>. It is supposed to be the cottage that Captain Cook lived in in England, however was moved stone by stone to Australia. Okay, maybe it is not the 'Theseus Paradox' namely because the original stones and thatch are being moved as opposed to being replaced, however the original cottage was in England but it is now in the middle of a park in Melbourne, so is it the same cottage considering the location is basically on the other side of the world. Well, my position in this case is that it is not the same cottage, but a replica that has been built with the materials that comprised of the original cottage – the original cottage, in my mind, has been destroyed.<br /><br />	Anyway, that is beside the point, even though the idea was determining whether the Scone of Stone was the real Scone of Stone (and if you are not sure how to pronounce the word scone, just check out <a href="https://youtu.be/F8G1xBJLzsc" rel="nofollow noopener">this Goodies Episode</a>, there were other ideas in here as well, such as trade deals, oil (which is supposed to be the fat of the Elephant) and of course the tussles that occur between the dwarves and trolls (though we also have werewolves and vampires as well). The thing with the Uberwald is that it is supposed to be, in one sense, Eastern Europe, which is Europe but somewhat backward compared to Western Europe (though my closest experience of Eastern Europe would be Praque, and Greece, but Greece is technically the Balkans).<br /><br />	Anyway, I have to admit that I really don't feel to enthusiastic about writing much more on this book because it really didn't do all that much to inspire me, though I have to admit that it would be good to see them turn more of Pratchet's books into a live action television show in the same vein that they did with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/601238.The_Colour_of_Magic__Discworld___1_" title="The Colour of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Colour of Magic</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34506.The_Light_Fantastic__Discworld___2__Rincewind__2_" title="The Light Fantastic (Discworld, #2; Rincewind #2) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Light Fantastic</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18178315323164999169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1986278883829430281">Please allow me one quick soul-searching moment. Before I was introduced to the awesomeness of Discworld…I was just an empty shell of a fan<br/><br/>I haven’t picked up Discworld book for quite some time (last one I read was Jingo) so reading the Fifth Elephant kind of gave me the warm and fuzzy feeling of falling in love with Sir Terry Pratchett’s work all over again. I think this book is the most action-packed volume in City Watch series yet. Imagine Bruce Willis all decked out in tights with British ac</span>
  <span id="freeText1986278883829430281" style="display:none">Please allow me one quick soul-searching moment. Before I was introduced to the awesomeness of Discworld…I was just an empty shell of a fan<br /><br />I haven’t picked up Discworld book for quite some time (last one I read was Jingo) so reading the Fifth Elephant kind of gave me the warm and fuzzy feeling of falling in love with Sir Terry Pratchett’s work all over again. I think this book is the most action-packed volume in City Watch series yet. Imagine Bruce Willis all decked out in tights with British accent and Ankh-Morpork sense of humor (and um, not so coiffuredly-challenged) and there you got Commander Vimes in all his glory. I must have cracked a few ribs laughing. There’s the motley crew of the Watch and a few new characters. The Igors really steal the show! (or sthill the thow, to be surgically precise) Also, Detritus and his Piecemaker is not the troll to be trifled with. I won’t go on about Nobby because then I wouldn’t be able to stop. The “hot pursuit” scene in the last chapter is hands down the coolest chase in police procedural history. John McClane himself can’t top that! Yippee ki yay little doggy;) </span>
